## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of concentration dA/dt as a function of concentration A and time t, which is the fundamental problem in chemical reaction kinetics. The rate law typically follows power-law dependence on concentration, with possible time-dependent effects from external forcing or coupled species whose concentrations vary in time.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = c0 * A (radioactive decay, unimolecular decomposition)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (bimolecular reaction of same species)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (generalized power-law rate law)
- Mixed-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (competing first and second order pathways)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme kinetics, saturation kinetics)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse reactions with equilibrium)
- Autocatalytic reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic-type autocatalysis)
- Langmuir-Hinshelwood: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A)**2 (surface-catalyzed reaction with competitive adsorption)
- Time-dependent rate with first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (time-varying rate constant, e.g., temperature ramp)
- Power-law with time modulation: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 * t**c2 (diffusion-limited kinetics with time dependence)
- Substrate inhibition: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A + c2 * A**2) (substrate inhibition in enzyme kinetics)
- Fractional order with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 (fractional order with constant source/sink)
- Cooperative kinetics (Hill-type): dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (c2 + A**c1) (cooperative binding/reaction)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope â†’ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects â†’ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay â†’ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior â†’ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects â†’ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Concentration power-law dependence â†’ dA/dt ~ A^n indicates reaction order n, reflecting molecularity of the elementary step
- Rational functions of concentration â†’ Saturation kinetics from enzyme or surface catalysis mechanisms where intermediates are in quasi-steady state
- Product of concentration and (constant - concentration) â†’ Autocatalytic or logistic behavior where both reactant and product participate
- Explicit time dependence in rate â†’ Suggests non-isothermal conditions, photochemical forcing, or elimination of coupled species whose concentration varies predictably with time
- Sum of multiple power-law terms in A â†’ Parallel reaction pathways with different orders competing simultaneously
- Negative coefficient on A terms â†’ Consumption/decay of species A (reactant disappearing)
- Square root or fractional power of A â†’ Chain reaction mechanisms or dissociative equilibrium preceding rate-limiting step
- Denominator polynomial in A â†’ Mechanistic rate law derived from quasi-steady-state approximation on reactive intermediates
